<p class="description">A life crisis causes a socialite to head to San Francisco, where she tries to reconnect with her sister.</p>
<p class="score"> Margaret: <img alt="three-and-a-half stars" class="rating" src="/web/20141224184752im_/http://www.abc.net.au/atthemovies/img/stars-three-and-a-half.png"/> David: <img alt="four-and-a-half stars" class="rating" src="/web/20141224184752im_/http://www.abc.net.au/atthemovies/img/stars-four-and-a-half.png"/> </p>

<div id="theReview">
<h2>Blue Jasmine</h2>
<p class="ratd"> Rated <em>M</em></p>
<p><em>Review by David Stratton</em></p>
<p>In Woody Allen's new film, CATE BLANCHETT plays Jasmine who flies first class from New York to San Francisco, talking non-stop to the stranger sitting next to her. She's come west to stay with her sister, Ginger, SALLY HAWKINS, though the siblings - adopted and with different birth parents - have little in common. Flashbacks show Jasmine was formerly married to Hal, ALEC BALDWIN, a New York wheeler-dealer; they had an apartment in the city and a house by the beach and Jasmine was part of the social whirl, unaware that Hal was a serial womaniser. All that has come crashing down, and Jasmine has to start life all over again, broke and in a strange city - it requires a great deal of readjustment.<br/><br/>I wouldn't be surprised to learn that Woody Allen saw Cate Blanchett in the stage production of A Streetcar Named Desire when it played in New York because there's something of Blanche Dubois in the story of Jasmine, a self-centred woman whose privileged lifestyle has come to an abrupt end and who now relies too much on booze and pills - and the comfort of strangers. She disapproves of her sister's 'loser' boyfriend, Bobby Cannavale, but then she also disapproved of Ginger's husband, the ebullient Augie, Andrew Dice Clay, who lost all his money thanks to Hal. Jasmine, like Blanche, is not always sympathetic, yet thanks to Cate Blanchett's soaring performance you do care for her as she makes one mistake after another. Sally Hawkins is wonderful, too - these two non-American actresses, one Australian, the other British, play Americans with complete conviction. The film is one of Allen's best in recent years, and beautifully shot in Scope, only the third time Allen has used the Scope format, after MANHATTAN and ANYTHING ELSE.</p>
<h2>Further comments</h2>
<p>DAVID: Margaret?<br/><br/>MARGARET: Well, you know my antennae go up with any Woody Allen film these days.<br/><br/>DAVID: Yes, and it upsets me that it does because it's not fair. <br/><br/>MARGARET: Well, it is fair in a way because you mention ANYTHING ELSE and that was the most misogynistic piece of cinema that has ever...<br/><br/>DAVID: That's a terrible film but that's not what we're discussing. We're discussing BLUE JASMINE.<br/><br/>MARGARET: No, but that's what set me on this path. Funny you should mention ANYTHING ELSE. I think there are simply wonderful performances. I think Woody Allen is famous for getting fabulous performances and I think mainly because of his writing. He does write good, meaty roles for people and everybody in this, including Andrew Dice Clay and Bobbie Cannavale, are really excellent. But there's a sense in me that I mourn the loss of Woody's romanticism, wry romanticism of his earlier films. Those films during the '70s, '80s, just about every single one was a gem. The last 20 years has been a lot patchier from him and I do feel that a certain cynicism has entered into his work?<br/><br/>DAVID: Yes, but hang on. One of your favourite films, in fact I think you chose it as a classic, was INTERIORS. <br/><br/>MARGARET: I know. <br/><br/>DAVID: And that was made right after ANNIE HALL and that was...<br/><br/>MARGARET: That was the great period of Woody Allen. <br/><br/>DAVID: Yes, but that's not a romantic story at all. That's a bleak story. <br/><br/>MARGARET: I know it is but it was wonderfully done. Not everybody liked that as much as I did.<br/><br/>DAVID: That's his Ingmar Bergman film.<br/><br/>MARGARET: I know. Yes, but you see, this is his Tennessee Williams' film.<br/><br/>DAVID: Yes, sure. <br/><br/>MARGARET: Just like MATCHPOINT was a steal from A PLACE IN THE SUN absolutely. <br/><br/>DAVID: Well, you say "a steal" but there's nothing wrong with that. I mean people have done new variations of Shakespeare. Kurosawa THRONE OF BLOOD, RAN. That's nothing new and you can't be angry with him for that.<br/><br/>MARGARET: No, I'm not angry with him for that. I'm disappointed. I think this is--<br/><br/>DAVID: Why? This is such a good film. This is a terrific film.<br/><br/>MARGARET: It is certainly a wonderful film in a lot of ways but I have my reservations.<br/><br/>DAVID: You have your prejudices, Margaret.<br/><br/>MARGARET: Well, maybe.<br/><br/>DAVID: We all do. <br/><br/>MARGARET: Can I mention Lars Von Trier? <br/><br/>DAVID: Yes. Hate him. <br/><br/>MARGARET: I'm giving this three and a half stars. <br/><br/>DAVID: I'm giving it four and a half. I really like this. <br/></p>

<p class="comment">((Blue Jasmine))[[3]]<br>My partner and I watched this together and the only thing that we couldn't quite agree on was whether to give it one or two stars. Did no-one else notice that the streets, seaside, township, party, high society people, jasmine, jasmines home etc all were in drab brown and  other colourless, depressed colours - cream, beige etc? The acting is overcooked, there is no discernible plot and any key narrative shifts are reliant on implausible chance meetings. The dialogue is plentiful and fast-flowing but devoid of any insight or humour. Noone in the audience at my inner-city, hip indi cinema laughed. <a id="m_ucMessageDisplay24399_m_anchMessageAnchor" name="m24399"></a>
<h3>Nicholas Dryad :</h3>
<p class="date">04 Oct 2013 8:22:46am</p>
<p class="comment">((Blue Jasmine))[[10]]<br/>It is a pity that we are frightened to see this film through 1980's style Marxist analysis. What we see is Allen returning to his examination of class through character  and persona. True, Blanchett plays Jasmine as an almost stereotyped 'northern' belle, but she becomes a Medea figure whose revenge wreaks pernicious havoc. As a result of her revenge, she has to share the fate of the people she inadvertently destroyed. The genius of the tight and muscular script makes this film a powerful morality play not the powerful cinema event that most Allen fans would like to relive.</p>
<p class="links">
<a href="https://web.archive.org/web/20141224184752/http://www2b.abc.net.au/tmb/View/AlertModerator.aspx?b=117&amp;m=24399&amp;tpa=&amp;r=%2ftmb%2fView%2fMessage.aspx%3fb%3d117%26t%3d796%26a%3d0%26ps%3d50%26tpa%3d%26uto%3d1%26dm%3d4%26ci%3d0%26pd%3d1%26so%3dDateTime%26soa%3dFalse%26p%3d1%26p2%3d0" onclick="return popup(this.href);">Alert moderator</a>

<h3>Hana :</h3>
<p class="date">03 Oct 2013 8:49:46pm</p>
<p class="comment">((Blue Jasmine))[[9]]<br/>An excellent film and brilliant performance from Cate Blanchett.  The inspiration for the film shouldn't really matter - I'm not sure at what point a piece of work becomes 'derivative' and therefore less worthy of praise. The film works wonderfully in portraying a soul lost to superficiality, materialism and the imperative of 'looking good' at all costs - the sickness of our times. Yet Jasmine as portrayed by Blanchett is never just a symbol. She is achingly convincing as a real human being. I liked this film much more than some of Allen's earlier films.</p>

<a id="m_ucMessageDisplay24308_m_anchMessageAnchor" name="m24308"></a>
<h3>David :</h3>
<p class="date">28 Sep 2013 1:30:43pm</p>
<p class="comment">((Blue Jasmine))[[10]]<br/>Masterpiece by my favorite filmmaker (despite a few duds). It works brilliantly on so many levels.<br/>A tribute (dazzling reinterpretation) to Streetcar Named Desire set in a city famed for its streetcars! Cute!<br/>Literally dozens of pitch-perfect performances - two sisters, husbands, boyfriends, (prospective) fiances, kids, dentist, socialites, blue-collar-guys...<br/>Beautiful scenery.<br/>Morality tale.<br/>Cynical, sardonic social satire.<br/>Meditation on the fragility (illusion?) of lasting love and happiness, and the essential loneliness of the human condition.<br/>And so much more - a totally unexpected twist elevates this story to the level of Shakespearean tragedy.<br/>One of Woody's nail clippings has more talent than a room of Oscar winners.</p>
<p class="links">
<a href="https://web.archive.org/web/20141224184752/http://www2b.abc.net.au/tmb/View/AlertModerator.aspx?b=117&amp;m=24308&amp;tpa=&amp;r=%2ftmb%2fView%2fMessage.aspx%3fb%3d117%26t%3d796%26a%3d0%26ps%3d50%26tpa%3d%26uto%3d1%26dm%3d4%26ci%3d0%26pd%3d1%26so%3dDateTime%26soa%3dFalse%26p%3d1%26p2%3d0" onclick="return popup(this.href);">Alert moderator</a>

<p class="comment">((Blue Jasmine))[[4]]<br/>You wouldn't think it was possible, but this Woody Allen film, despite pleasing the critics substantially, didn't do anything for me. The movie could almost be called a waste of time because the story has little trajectory besides the constant sadness of Jasmine. <h3>Brutus :</h3>
<p class="date">23 Sep 2013 3:58:13pm</p>
<p class="comment">((Blue Jasmine))[[9]]<br/>Streetcar Named Desire, updated for the modern world. Not a full-on comedy by any means, but pretty funny as well, whilst also being compelling. Cate is wonderful, though it is a good ensemble cast all around. Hard to watch sometimes, as the pretensions unfold and the psychological damage accumulates. Woody and Cate are merciless in their portrayal of an unpleasant woman's disintegration. Uncomfortable and insightful, but also with a kernel of hope for those who choose more honest approaches to life and relationships. Ultimately this is uplifting art by a great artist. Welcome back, Woody!</p>
<p class="links">
<a href="https://web.archive.org/web/20141224184752/http://www2b.abc.net.au/tmb/View/AlertModerator.aspx?b=117&amp;m=24231&amp;tpa=&amp;r=%2ftmb%2fView%2fMessage.aspx%3fb%3d117%26t%3d796%26a%3d0%26ps%3d50%26tpa%3d%26uto%3d1%26dm%3d4%26ci%3d0%26pd%3d1%26so%3dDateTime%26soa%3dFalse%26p%3d1%26p2%3d0" onclick="return popup(this.href);">Alert moderator</a>

<h3>Cupid Bowie :</h3>
<p class="date">17 Sep 2013 3:01:22pm</p>
<p class="comment">((Blue Jasmine))[[8]]<br/>This is a modern-day take on Tennesse Williams and also the GFC (read Maddoff) type of disasters that created havoc in the psyche of SOME of those at the 'top' of American Eastern Society. Blanchett is brilliant: a fading New York socialite who has hit rock bottom; her sister Ginger (Sally Hawkins) gives a perfectly nuanced performance as the "less-favoured sister" and supporting roles from the remainder of the cast, in particular Bobby Cannavale, are superb. <a id="m_ucMessageDisplay24095_m_anchMessageAnchor" name="m24095"></a>
<h3>Steve Manders :</h3>
<p class="date">16 Sep 2013 12:42:07am</p>
<p class="comment">((Blue Jasmine))[[7]]<br/>This captivating film recalled Adam Hills' favourite German word schadenfreude to me: satisfaction at the misfortunes of others. There is something awkwardly satisfying about seeing others stuff up their lives more spectacularly than you have so far.  Cate Blanchett is the lucky recipient of great material, from which she delivers a tour de force of Jasmine in all her ups and downs.  Jasmine and Ginger are unrelated adoptees of the same family with little in common .  Except their highly variable need for each other, prompted by immediate need and the vagaries of the men in their lives.</p>
<p class="links">
<a href="https://web.archive.org/web/20141224184752/http://www2b.abc.net.au/tmb/View/AlertModerator.aspx?b=117&amp;m=24095&amp;tpa=&amp;r=%2ftmb%2fView%2fMessage.aspx%3fb%3d117%26t%3d796%26a%3d0%26ps%3d50%26tpa%3d%26uto%3d1%26dm%3d4%26ci%3d0%26pd%3d1%26so%3dDateTime%26soa%3dFalse%26p%3d1%26p2%3d0" onclick="return popup(this.href);">Alert moderator</a>

<p class="comment">((Blue Jasmine))[[9]]<br/>Allen in great form and back I'm the USA after his European sojourn, but on the west coast, far from his New York comfort zone.<br/>This is " A Streetcar Named Desire", reinterpreted seventy years later and I loved it.<br/>It is a virtuoso piece for Blanchett, and she plays it for all it's worth. <script language="JavaScript" type="text/javascript">


var newtopicKey;

$(document).ready(function(){

audShow();
changeAction();
formatComments();

// end ready
});	

function audShow() {
	// display word count only if js enabled
	document.getElementById("wordCount").style.display='inline';
	document.getElementById("audiencecomment").style.display='block';
	if (document.getElementById("allnewComments")) {
		document.getElementById("allnewComments").innerHTML = document.getElementById("loadComments").innerHTML;
	}
}


function changeAction() {
	// avoids non-js form submission 
	var tmpStoryid = "??StoryID??";
	if (document.m_frmMainForm) {
		document.m_frmMainForm.action = 'https://web.archive.org/web/20141224184752/http://www2b.abc.net.au/tmb/View/NewMessage.aspx?b=117&amp;tn='+tmpStoryid+'&amp;dm=1&amp;tpa=&amp;r=&amp;layout=popup';
		}
}



function formatComments() {
	// replace H3 tag with 'Name:' + name
	var arrayH3 = document.getElementById("comments").getElementsByTagName("h3");
	for (var i = 0; i < arrayH3.length; i++) {
		var theString = arrayH3[i].innerHTML;
		theString = theString.replace(":", "");
		theString = "Name: "+theString;
		arrayH3[i].innerHTML = 	theString;
	}
	// add rating value to each comment
	var arrayComment = getElementsByClassName( 'comment', 'p' );	
	for (var c = 0; c < arrayComment.length; c++) {
		var theComment = arrayComment[c].innerHTML;
		theComment = theComment.replace("[[", "<span class='userRating'>Rating: <img src='https://web.archive.org/web/20141224184752/http://www.abc.net.au/atthemovies/audience/stars").replace("]]",".png' alt='rating'></span>").replace("((", "<!-- ").replace(")))", "))").replace("))", "-->");
		arrayComment[c].innerHTML = theComment;
	}

	
}


function formCheck(zeForm) {
	// pass key to form
	document.getElementById("keyField").value = newtopicKey;
	// basic validation
	if (document.getElementById("yname").value.length < 1) {
		alert("Please enter your name or nickname.");
		document.getElementById("yname").style.background='#FFFDC8';
		return false;
	}
	if (document.getElementById("yemail").value.length < 6) {
		alert("Please enter a valid email address.");
		document.getElementById("yemail").style.background='#FFFDC8';
		return false;
	}
	if (zeForm.score.options[0].selected && zeForm.score.options[0].value=="na") {
		alert("You forgot to rate the movie!");
		document.getElementById("score").style.background='#FFFDC8';	
		return false;
	}	
	// check for http
	spamcheck=zeForm.m_tbxText.value;
	if (spamcheck.indexOf("http")!=-1) {
		document.m_frmMainForm.action = 'https://web.archive.org/web/20141224184752/http://www.abc.net.au/atthemovies/audience/blank.htm';
	}
	// check word count
	wct = cnt(zeForm.m_tbxText.value);
	if (wct > 100) {
		alert("Comments are limited to 100 words. You've written "+wct+" words!");
		document.getElementById("remark").style.background='#FFFDC8';
		return false;	
	}
	
	// replace usual suspect bad characters 
	badChars = Array  ('', '', '', '', '', 'ö', 'é', 'è', 'ñ', 'â', ' ', '','','´');
	goodChars = Array ('...', '-', '-', '"', '"', 'o', 'e', 'e', 'n', 'a', ' ', '\'','\'','\'');
	fld = document.getElementById("remark");
	for(i=0;i<badChars.length;i++){
		restring = new RegExp( badChars[i] , 'g');
		fld.value = fld.value.replace(restring,goodChars[i]);
	}
	fldn = document.getElementById("yname");
	for(j=0;j<badChars.length;j++){
		restringj = new RegExp( badChars[j] , 'g');
		fldn.value = fldn.value.replace(restringj,goodChars[j]);
	}	
	
	// add rating to comment field in [[ ]] tags 
	var theSel = zeForm.score.selectedIndex;
	var theRating = zeForm.score[theSel].value; 
	zeForm.m_tbxText.value = "[["+theRating+"]]\n" + zeForm.m_tbxText.value;
	
	// add movie title to comment field in (( )) tags 
	zeForm.m_tbxText.value = "(("+theMovie+"))" + zeForm.m_tbxText.value;	
	
	// display thankyou div layer and hide form. 
	document.getElementById("favFormThx").style.display='block';
	document.getElementById("favForm").style.display='none';
	document.getElementById("wordCount").style.display='none';	
	
	// all clear, submit the form
	return true;
}

// word count function
function cnt(theform){
	var y=theform;
	var r = 0;
	a=y.replace('\n',' ');
	a=a.split(' ');
	for (z=0; z<a.length; z++) {if (a[z].length > 0) r++;}
	return r;
}

function remainingWords(textAreaContent,textAreaContentValue, maxWords) 
{
	// Determine the number of words we have left
	var numberofwords = cnt(textAreaContentValue);
	wordsLeft = maxWords - numberofwords;
	if (wordsLeft < 1)
	{	// if 100 change color to red
		document.getElementById("wcNum").style.color='red'; 
	} else {
		document.getElementById("wcNum").style.color='#ffffff'; 
	}
	// update word count number
	document.getElementById("wcNum").innerHTML=(0+numberofwords);
}

// windows media alt box
function showWindows() {
	document.getElementById("windowsMed").style.display='block';
}


// generic get by class name
function getElementsByClassName(strClass, strTag, objContElm) {
  strTag = strTag || "*";
  objContElm = objContElm || document;    
  var objColl = objContElm.getElementsByTagName(strTag);
  if (!objColl.length &&  strTag == "*" &&  objContElm.all) objColl = objContElm.all;
  var arr = new Array();                              
  var delim = strClass.indexOf('|') != -1  ? '|' : ' ';   
  var arrClass = strClass.split(delim);    
  for (var i = 0, j = objColl.length; i < j; i++) {                         
    var arrObjClass = objColl[i].className.split(' ');   
    if (delim == ' ' && arrClass.length > arrObjClass.length) continue;
    var c = 0;
    comparisonLoop:
    for (var k = 0, l = arrObjClass.length; k < l; k++) {
      for (var m = 0, n = arrClass.length; m < n; m++) {
        if (arrClass[m] == arrObjClass[k]) c++;
        if ((delim == '|' && c == 1) || (delim == ' ' && c == arrClass.length)) {
          arr.push(objColl[i]); 
          break comparisonLoop;
        }
      }
    }
  }
  return arr; 
}

// called from 'new discussion' page in iframe
function sayHello(theKey) {
	newtopicKey = theKey;
}

// talk to www2b iframe
document.domain = "abc.net.au";

</script>

		//mobile device supports m3u8 html5 HLS video	
		$("#flashplayer").html("<video id='tvVideo' width='598' height='336' poster='/atthemovies/img/2013/ep29/jasmine_large.jpg' controls autoplay><source src='https://web.archive.org/web/20141224184752/http://tvmpint-vh.akamaihd.net/i/tv/streams/atthemovies/20130913_bluejasmine,,.mp4.csmil/master.m3u8' type='video/mp4' />Your browser does not support the video tag.</video>");

// end ready
});
